Education News

The Ministry of Education Starts Compiling Curriculum Outlines for Universities

To adapt to the University Entrance Examination in the 27th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1938]

After the Ministry of Education compiled and announced the curriculum standards for primary and secondary schools in general education, as well as the curriculum or teaching material outlines for normal schools and vocational schools, it began working on the curriculum for various colleges in universities for higher education last year, starting with medicine. It has already convened the Medical Education Committee several times to discuss the draft curriculum standards for medical colleges, etc. After the members revised and sorted it out, the Ministry of Education will convene another meeting soon to make the final decision. The Ministry of Education had already started the second step, which was to compile the curriculum for other colleges in universities. The Examination Yuan informed the Quanshu Conference [a conference on personnel evaluation and appointment] that universities would hold an entrance examination in the 27th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1938], and urged them to compile university curriculum standards in advance to adapt to the examination. Based on its predetermined plan, the Ministry of Education has now drafted curriculum outlines for various colleges in universities and has replied to the Examination Yuan, explaining that it is in the process of compiling the curriculum outlines. It is found that the compilation of university curriculum was already done in the 19th year of the Republic [i.e., 1930]. At that time, the detailed content of the curriculum for various subjects in universities was listed one by one, which was relatively complicated, and it was more difficult for universities to implement it. It is heard that the outlines drafted this time are more concrete and easier to implement universally.

Bankruptcy of Local Education in Zhejiang Province

Director Xu Shaodi of the Department of Education Eloquently Narrates the Reasons and Remedial Measures

Xu Shaodi, Director of the Department of Education of Zhejiang Province, reported on how to protect local education funding at the Provincial Government Memorial Weekly yesterday. He said that what he wanted to talk about today was the issue of local education funding. Due to disasters and other reasons last year, local education funding had reached the point of bankruptcy. The number of primary schools closed in various counties reached more than 1,000. In total, the counties under the three old prefectures in western Zhejiang were short of 690,000 yuan, and the eight old prefectures in eastern Zhejiang were short of more than 1.1 million yuan. It is important to note here that the funding for district-established and private primary schools is not included. Since funding is so short, most of the existing businesses cannot be maintained. Currently, more than 70 or 80 primary schools have been closed in Jiangshan, Tonglu, Dongyang, and other counties. Yuhang, Shangyu, Tangxi, Chun'an, Sui'an, and other counties also have 40 or 50 primary schools that have not been able to open. The educational funding owed by various counties is at least four or five months, and at most eight or nine months. As for the subsidy for township primary schools, Qu County has owed it for as long as three years. The personnel serving in primary schools already have a very difficult life. When they encounter this kind of double whammy, the depth of their pain can be imagined. If human beings have not lost their sympathy, they will pay close attention to these educational personnel who are suffering. The reasons why local education funding is so difficult are very complex. The total education fee in the province is about 3.3 million yuan, of which about 2.2 million yuan belongs to the land tax and school field rent. Therefore, once there is a famine and the land tax is not collected, education will be shaken. Last year's drought caused the harvest in various counties to be only 40%, and the education fee would be short by a huge 1.3 million yuan. Therefore, poor harvest is the primary reason for the shortage of education fee. Secondly, the decline of the rural areas over the years has affected the general rural economy, and various education funds have decreased accordingly. This is the second reason. The county magistrates or financial institutions in various counties often misappropriate education fees. This is the third reason. The collection of donations and taxes and the management of school property inevitably involve embezzlement or other corrupt practices. This is the fourth reason. The budget is inaccurate, the false list is too long, or the expansion is excessive, and the expenditure exceeds the amount. Therefore, the income and expenditure do not match, and it becomes more and more exhausted. This is the fifth reason. The provincial funds allocated have already been discounted twice, and now they have to be tightened, and the actual receipt is only 50%. This is the sixth reason. Various places have been ordered to abolish harsh taxes, but at the same time, there is no supplementary funding. This is the seventh reason. The local education fees in this province are as described above. If we do not take urgent measures, we will inevitably go bankrupt. On the one hand, we are shouting about popularizing education and eliminating illiteracy, but now we cannot even maintain the existing education business, which is too contradictory. I think we can only talk about emergency relief and maintenance at present. I hope that the Department of Finance can quickly transfer one million public bonds to the management committee so that the relief business can be carried out. As for the active work, I hope that all education circles in the province and all enthusiastic people from all walks of life will mobilize. 1. To ensure that education fee income is guaranteed, each county should follow the province's education fee guarantee method and try to make the education fee independent. Under the principle of unified collection and unified expenditure, designate reliable income as a special fund for education fees. 2. Actively reorganize local education funds and property, strictly define management methods, so that they will not be controlled and swallowed by a few people, or used by other agencies. 3. Encourage donations to establish schools, so that words, property, and private property can be transformed into school property in large quantities. 4. Carry out education savings. There are more than 700,000 primary school students in the province. If each person saves half a yuan each year, there are more than 20,000 primary school teachers. If they save one yuan, and students and faculty members in county and municipal middle schools total about 8,000, if each person saves one and a half yuan, they can get more than 10,000 yuan, a total of more than 400,000 yuan a year. If you accumulate it for ten years, you can get more than 4 million yuan. After 50 years, it can increase to several million yuan. By then, the interest income will be enough. 5. Carry out a donation campaign to raise local education fees. Each county will carry out it separately. I think there must be many people who are happy to donate. All of this donation will be allocated as a foundation and will never be used for other purposes. The above are several ways to protect local education funding. I hope that all people in the province will rise up and strive for it. I also hope that the education sector can bravely take the lead and work together to protect this matter.

General Evaluation Report of the National Labor Exhibition (5)

(3) The primary school labor curriculum standards place great emphasis on utilizing local specialties and raw materials. However, there were not many such products in this exhibition. Even famous raw materials, such as Yixing's pottery clay, Jiangxi's porcelain clay, and Shandong's wheat straw, were not seen to be fully utilized to make products (except for vocational school products). Only a few types of products paid attention to utilizing local raw materials, including the stone carvings from Lai County Middle School and Shengquan Primary School in Huang County, Shandong, the bamboo products from the Second Provincial Primary School in Fujian, and the wool products from Qinghai and Gansu.

(4) Applying wisdom to construct objects is the most important condition in craft manufacturing. The ability of manufactured goods to innovate and change with each passing day is the product of applying this principle. There were many exhibits with this condition in this exhibition. The most prominent was the primary school in Fujian, which used a copper coin as raw material to make badges, buttons, and various small copper objects easily, which showed ingenuity. The Autonomous Primary School and Women's Vocational School in Hunan also made vases by connecting buttons, which was also very delicate. The pocket-sized surveying instrument from Xingye Middle School in Guangxi had a simple manufacturing method and a legal structure. The alarm bell from Bowei Primary School in Shandong used electricity to sound an alarm, and there was also an electric lock that used electricity to lock the door, which was quite thoughtful and practical. The Zhenshi Attached Primary School of Jiangsu Province used chicken and duck eggshells with bright, dark, strong, and light colors to embed portraits, using ordinary waste products to achieve this elegant and beautiful result, which was also innovative. The wooden weighing scale from the 15th Primary School in the provincial capital of Anhui, the wooden balance and mousetrap from the Jiangjundu Primary School in the provincial capital of Jiangxi, and the various animal models made of thin pine branches and thick pine segments by the Fifth Municipal Primary School in Hankou, Hubei, all had wonderful ideas and ingenious structures.

(5) There were very few inventions of teaching aids and other machinery in this exhibition. Only Ling Junping's spring abacus (Jiading Ordinary Primary School) and Gengfu's waterwheel (Huaiyin Normal School of Jiangsu Province) were still meaningful. The spring abacus invented by Ling Jun was even more of a high-quality finished product that closely met practical applications and should be encouraged.

(6) The scope of the primary school labor curriculum standard is very wide. Therefore, the labor skills learned by normal school students should cover the entire primary school curriculum. However, there are many problems with the implementation period, such as how to achieve this goal. It is still a problem that needs to be studied. Here, we see the basic production method samples of various crafts from Huangjiashi Primary School in Anhui and the craft composition samples from Jiaxing Middle School in Zhejiang (there are also some in other places, here are just examples). The basic production methods of the craft part of the primary school curriculum are all included. If you learn it, you can completely understand the basic methods of the entire curriculum. Therefore, the craft of normal school students can be based on the above materials as the core teaching materials, and then select toys, teaching aids, and instruments related to primary school education for application. Then, the purpose of teaching, application, and learning time can be solved.

(7) Although there were many teaching materials related to national defense in this exhibition, except for the national defense design of He'an Primary School in Shanghai, which was more meaningful, other schools only made a few models of cannons, guns, airplanes, and warships, which were of little value. In the future, we should pay attention to the construction of trenches, civil air defense, poison gas protection, and other supplies and models according to the students' level, so as to give students a deep impression and be more applicable.

(8) Various materials used in the labor science and various working processes, such as specimens, are necessary reference materials for labor teaching. However, there are no ready-made products for sale in our country at present. It all depends on the schools collecting and manufacturing them at ordinary times. The normal school labor materials should take these reference materials as an important work so that students can make their own teaching aids when they serve in primary schools after graduation. However, in this exhibition, only Jiaxing Middle School in Zhejiang and Huangjiashi Primary School collected, produced, completed, and organized according to the labor science curriculum standards, which should be rewarded.

(9) Very few industrial products in this exhibition were accompanied by work drawings drawn by students themselves. According to the labor teaching in our country's schools, the production of handicrafts is mostly done arbitrarily without drawing work drawings first. Therefore, before the finished product is completed, the author's intention and the form of the finished product are often unknown to others. Therefore, students not only cannot draw formal work drawings but also cannot recognize them, which has a great impact on the future of industrial improvement in our country. In the future, labor science and handicraft production should pay attention to work drawings to cultivate students' drawing and drawing recognition abilities.

(10) Small bamboo handicrafts are almost the most common products. It is estimated that their quantity is the crown of all products. The reason for this phenomenon is that although labor education has been repeatedly promoted by the government, the number of schools that actually pay attention to and implement it is still very small. Under this state, schools have no tool equipment to facilitate work, and families have no materials to supply for practice. Therefore, they can only use hand knives to scrape bamboo slices and carve bamboo slices. There is no other good way. Therefore, there are many bamboo products. However, these achievements, although they take a lot of effort, have very little effect. If our country wants to seek labor education and labor production, we must find ways to remedy the shortcomings in equipment.

(11) Stone carvings and seals seem to be works of art and should not be included in labor science teaching. Exquisite instrument models, display models, school building models, and sports models (except for those required for teaching design) are not in the minority of products. Although they have some labor value, they have no practical value. It is a pity to spend useful materials and valuable time on this kind of work. Using time-consuming and energy-intensive embroidery as teaching materials for ordinary middle schools (except for vocational schools) does not seem to be very consistent with the main purpose of labor. Sewing only pays attention to western-style single clothes and embroidered pillows, ignoring the ordinary sewing methods of ordinary shoes, hats, and cotton-padded clothes, which fails to properly adapt to the daily life of the common people. It is hoped that the sixth provision of the teaching rules in the curriculum standard will organize the teaching materials and reduce the malpractices of "fragmentation," "mixing," and "repetition." However, 80% to 90% of the products in this exhibition are still disorganized and individual objects. In terms of teaching, there is no clue of contact research to be found. In terms of production, there is no progress to be found in the practice design. This phenomenon should be improved as soon as possible. The above points are of great importance to the implementation of labor facilities and curriculum and are specially put forward for research.

(12) Carved pen holders and wooden screen joints were also numerous throughout the hall. Judging from their work, the time and economy spent were considerable. Considering their use, the gain is not worth the loss. In terms of its value, in addition to training clumsy and dead work spirit, there is nothing else to be taken. This type of teaching material is not very suitable. If the second labor exhibition is held, I hope not to see it again.

(13) Using several colored papers to cut and paste into several pictures is a teaching material in the art curriculum, but in this exhibition, some people used it to fill in the achievements of labor. This facility not only violates the curriculum standards but also has no labor value. It only wastes children's time between paste, paper, and silk. Therefore, it seems appropriate to prohibit it in the future. In addition, using colored wool threads and simple needlework to embroider pillowcases, lifting lists, and other large and small items is slightly more valuable than cutting and pasting. However, if the object is small and can be made in only two or three hours, and it is occasionally done, there is nothing wrong with it. If it is a large object, it takes the whole semester to complete it. Then, the child's body and mind are bound by the rigid work, and the harm cannot be overstated. Therefore, it also seems appropriate to limit it.

(14) Some of the products are very neatly made, but when you look at their forms, structures, colors, etc., it seems that they are made by one or two people. Although the product list fills in that a certain item is produced by School A, a certain item is produced by School B, a certain item is produced by primary school, a certain item is produced by normal school, and the types are similar, the forms are similar, and the structure colors are not much different, it is difficult to investigate what kind of method is used to implement teaching. After the production is completed, it is gathered and sent to the meeting. This type of product whose source is unknown can only be placed in the list of non-discussion and non-discussion during the evaluation. There are also some with good themes and good production, but the level is very different. For example, there is a warship in a certain school in a certain province. At first glance, it should be a cooperative achievement of junior high school students, but its label states that it is the achievement of a certain grade in junior primary school. This type of product, regardless of its authenticity, regardless of its merits and demerits, is also not discussed. There are also products whose style and skills are clearly from the hands of craftsmen. Even if the theme is good and the level is appropriate, it is not discussed. However, there are also those who are retained as reference products because of their good themes.

(2) Sub-evaluation (in the order of display)

(1) Shandong Province has many self-made teaching aids (simple physics and chemistry instruments and biological specimen models, etc.) and can use local products or rural by-products to make practical products, which are numerous and useful (stoneware, grass curtains, reed curtains, willow baskets, wheat straw hats, mountain thorn baskets, etc.). It can be seen that they can pay attention to the labor production and education of the common people and strive to implement it. But it is a pity that there are too few ordinary educational toys in its products.

(2) Hebei Province has many self-made teaching aids (simple physics and chemistry instruments, geographical models, building blocks, etc.) and educational toys. The achievements of metalwork are particularly good. It can be seen that each school in its products has considerable equipment, but it lacks products for the common people.

(3) There are many wood and bamboo works in Beijing, and most of them are small practical products. The clay sculptures of various ethnic groups' masks, with ten styles, are very good and meaningful.

(4) Henan Province has many good wooden practical products and toys. There are many national defense teaching aids or toys. Other teaching aids (physics, chemistry, biology, specimen models, and mechanical prototypes, etc.) are also numerous and generally applicable. The clay potting and kiln products (plain fired and glazed) are very good, but there are few products for the common people.

(5) Nanjing City can develop various crafts on average, so all kinds of products should be available. Among them, teaching aids and practical products are the majority. The various products in the city are novel and applicable, and there are many creative designs. In terms of teaching, it can pay attention to the design of large units and the working process. In the structure and form of various works, it can also pay attention to correctness and beauty. Especially those with national defense (such as going to the front line to design, etc.) and scientific (such as "volcano model," etc.) spirit are the most distinctive.

Sun Fuyuan Agrees with the Principles of the Ten Declarations

Advocates that National Spirit Cannot Be Without a Place to Rest

Seeks National Revival, Most Wary of Blindly Following

Mr. Sun Fuyuan, Director of the Literature Department of the Chinese Association for the Promotion of Mass Education, returned to Beijing from his hometown of Shaoxing to visit relatives. When he passed through Shanghai, someone asked him what he thought of the Chinese-based cultural construction movement. He expressed his agreement, saying that he had been feeling a lot about the issue of Chinese-based culture in recent years, and had repeatedly published articles, arguing that most of his views were the same as those of the ten people. He also listed several examples to illustrate his personal views, generally saying that culture is like the customs of a nation, each with its own historical origin and its own conditions for existence. There is no need to force them to be the same, and there is no absolute standard of superiority or inferiority among various customs, nor is there any reason to imitate them blindly. As for the scope of Western culture, it only accounts for a quarter of the world's land and population. The other three-quarters of the nations, apart from the natives of Western colonies, have no obligation to follow Western culture entirely. Moreover, our country has a culture passed down for four or five thousand years, which is different from uncivilized nations, and there is no need to abandon ourselves and follow others. In short, the strengths of the West should be adopted as much as possible, and our own strengths should be brought into full play as much as possible. Our own shortcomings should be eliminated as much as possible, and the shortcomings of the West should also be avoided as much as possible. For example, the spiritual life of the French nation is almost entirely entrusted to the tightly organized Catholic Church, while in China, since the end of the Qing Dynasty, as a result of destroying temples, the spiritual life of the nation's rural farmers has had no place to rest. All foreign doctrines such as communism and anarchism are like entering a no-man's land. This cannot but blame the scholars of reform at that time for not recognizing the culture of their own country and acting rashly. We cannot but eat the consequences today. Another example is dancing. Western dancing was originally a rural custom, which was transformed into dances such as the foxtrot in the city, with clear origins and became a habit. However, it is incomprehensible that Chinese youth must also follow suit. There are countless other blind actions, and our solid culture is shelved. How can our country achieve national revival with this situation, and so on. It is said that Mr. Sun also expressed to others that after he goes north, he will do his best to promote the concretization of the ten-person declaration.

Principal Dispute at Cangxiang Elementary School in Beijing

Principal Wei of Cangxiang Elementary School in Beijing took over the school amidst the chaos. In the past two years, he has reorganized and expanded the school, and the results are obvious. Principal Wei argued on the grounds that the faculty and staff had no security and found it difficult to hand over the school.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits

— (Kuang Dai)

The term "tidbits" is very important and should not be ignored, especially in medicine, where it should be given more attention. The day before yesterday, according to Dr. Zhang: "There is a patient in my hospital who was injured in the abdomen by a knife, and the intestines and peritoneum have leaked out. After the chief surgeon performed the operation, he sent him back to his hometown, and at the same time sewed up the wound so that it would no longer leak out. However, because this person lost too much blood, the situation is very dangerous, so a drip method is used to allow the physiological saline to enter the heart drop by drop from the vein, flow back to the artery, and be used by all the tissues of the body. The effect is to replenish blood to maintain the patient's life, and it can also resist toxins. However, this method must be used properly. It is limited to a few points or drops per minute. If it is excessive, the patient will not only not benefit, but will harm his life." Is this tidbit not very important in medicine? I hope that my country's new medical colleagues will pay attention to this tidbit and not regard human life as a child's play.

Collector

— Zhou Xian

The term "collector" is very popular these days. In the past few years, I only heard people say "collecting stamps," which was quite interesting. In addition, it was only the students in the school who carried collecting boxes, collected a few plants, caught a few insects, and collected a few pieces of rock debris, and returned to the school to make some specimens of animals, plants, and minerals. It seems that I have never heard of anything else.

But in recent years, there are more and more people who love to collect. As far as the friends I know are concerned, there are also several who are very fond of making very systematic collections.

One is fond of collecting cigarette packs. He has only been collecting cigarette packs for four years, but he has already collected more than 370 kinds. His method of collecting is to go to the cigarette shop on the alley every day to ask if there are any new cigarettes on the market. If there are, he will buy a pack regardless of whether they are Chinese or foreign, expensive or cheap. Therefore, recently, when the cigarette shop has new products, they always invite him to buy them. This friend does not smoke himself, so he always asks people to smoke the cigarettes he buys, but he has this strange interest.

A certain gentleman is a collector of counterfeit banknotes. It is said that he has been collecting for more than ten years, but he has not collected 100 kinds. However, his interest in collecting has been the same for more than ten years and has never waned. No matter who he meets, he will ask, "Have you been cheated by any counterfeit banknotes these days?" If the newspaper publishes a piece of news about "cracking down on a counterfeit banknote organization," he will be very active in wanting to collect a fresh pattern.

There is also one who specializes in collecting Chinese medicine prescriptions. He has been collecting for two years, and there are already five or six hundred prescriptions in his home (one prescription per doctor). No matter who he goes to, he always inquires if anyone has been ill. If there is, he will ask for the prescription. His income and expenditure were not very generous. However, he always has to spend five or six yuan a month to ask unknown Chinese medicine doctors to prescribe prescriptions. Because of this, his wife often scolds him for being crazy and often quarrels with him, but he still collects them. He said that in three years, he can collect the prescriptions of 1,000 doctors.

Wild Duck Hunting Tales

— A. Yang

Wild ducks are another name for teal, resembling ducks but capable of high flight. They are gregarious and often inhabit lakes and marshes, as in Du Fu's poem, "Ducklings sleep beside their mother on the sand." Their plumage is beautiful, especially the males, as in Zhou Zizhi's poem, "Mallards follow the green waves." Their bodies are plump and fatty, the meat is edible and delicious, and they have abundant down feathers, light and warm, which can be used to make clothing, quilts, and bedding, making them prized items for warding off the cold.

My Suzhou's Dongting Lake, Sha Lake, Yangcheng Lake, and other places produce many wild ducks. Every winter, or when the spring ice first melts, many hunters make a living by hunting wild ducks. The hunting guns used by these people are called "one-eyed blunderbusses," each weighing over a hundred pounds. When hunting, they usually go in pairs, with two boats, one large and one small. They first load the gun onto the small boat, and then place the small boat on the large boat, like a lifeboat attached to a large ship. Every morning or evening, they put the gun boat into the water, with one person lying down. When they see flocks of wild ducks feeding by the lakeshore, they aim and fire the gun, obtaining dozens or hundreds of birds in one shot. The bullets are called "iron pellets." The method of making iron pellets is as follows: first, melt pig iron in a furnace, and at the same time prepare a wooden basin filled with cold water, with smooth objects like pumpkins or yams placed in the middle. After the molten iron is taken out, it is poured directly onto the pumpkins, etc. Immediately, molten sparks fly everywhere, and upon entering the cold water, they become iron pellets. The skill of the makers varies greatly; skilled makers produce perfectly round pellets, while unskilled makers produce oval or flat pellets, which are unusable. The iron pellets must be dried after being taken out of the water to prevent rusting. Their value is about seven or eight yuan per dan (unit of weight), while pig iron is only one or two yuan per dan. Comparing the above, the thickness of the profit is evident!

New Benevolence?

Kerosene Can

— Yan B.G.

The facilities in the city are more complete than those in the countryside and towns. For example, these past two days we have often heard reports of fires in various places. In the long night, when good dreams are at their peak, we are often awakened by several alarm bells from the watchtower, and at the same time we hear the clanging bells of the fire trucks rushing to the scene. If the distance is slightly closer, we hurriedly put on our clothes, walk to the balcony, and look outside, only to see the fire shining brightly, sparks flying into the dark sky, already forming a prairie fire. Cries and shouts can also be heard from afar, and my heart sometimes pounds like a frightened deer. I then turn around, put on my clothes, pull open the door, and go to the disaster site to make a pilgrimage.

Old, young, men, and women are all huddled next to the things they have carried out, tears streaming down their faces, staring blankly at a pile of rubble. It is truly a miserable sight!

But in the countryside and towns, when a fire breaks out, all one hears is the sound of kerosene cans being banged everywhere, shaking the whole town. In the cold winter season, getting up is relatively slow. Ten or so people carry a water dragon to the place where the fire is burning, set up the nozzle, assign people to pump the bellows, and assign people to fetch water. By the time the nozzle produces water, everything has already turned to ashes, and even collapsed, or one fire has even spread to dozens of homes! It is truly suffering from the lack of adequate facilities. However, every household must hang an empty kerosene can on their door in order to sleep soundly. This iron can has a kind of wonderful use: first, it can replace the fire alarm bell; second, it can prevent thieves from digging through the door, as it will fall to the ground and awaken the owner. Therefore, a kerosene can sells for three silver dollars each in the countryside and towns.

Vegetable Root Flavors

— Jin X.Y.

Vegetables are essential ingredients for dishes. Although they are available in all four seasons, they are especially good in winter. Once they have been exposed to heavy frost, their flavor becomes even more delicious. They are not only known for their palatability, but their natural nourishment is extremely suitable for the human body, which is especially rare. The following four types of vegetables are the most prominent in winter.

(1) Cabbage: Cabbage is a top-grade vegetable, a variant of su, which the Tang people called "broad-leaved Wu su." It is called su because it does not wither in winter and is commonly seen in all four seasons, having the qualities of a pine tree. Cabbage originally came from Jiaozhou, Shandong, commonly called Jiaocai. The soil in Shandong is loose and the weather is dry, so it was originally unsuited to the local soil and water. Later, it was cultivated by artificial means. The cabbages sold on the market today are mostly produced locally. The shape of cabbage is as follows: the leaves and stalks are both flat and broad, tightly wrapped layer upon layer, the whole forming a cylindrical shape, with the top resembling a spherical shape. The leaves are slightly yellowish. Late autumn and early winter are the times of its initial peak production. Once exposed to heavy frost, its texture becomes soft and its flavor is especially sweet. It can be cooked with fish, meat, shrimp, crab, raw fish, hot pot, etc., as an essential ingredient. When cooked with dried small shrimp (dried shrimp), it is called "golden hook cabbage." When the heart of the cabbage is stuffed with thousand-cut meat, wrapped layer upon layer, tied with netting, and cooked with chicken broth or Nanjing ham, it is called "cabbage pagoda." The freshness of its soup and the sweetness of its taste are not inferior to top-grade delicacies. There is also a type of cabbage with loose leaves, green on the outside and tender yellow on the inside, produced in western Zhejiang, with a slightly inferior taste. Furthermore, there is a type with completely green petal tips, not tightly wrapped, forming a long, oval shape, which is even less a true type of cabbage. Its nature is very stiff, difficult to cook until tender, and the taste is also vastly different.

(2) Plate-shaped Cabbage: It is called plate-shaped cabbage because it grows flat on the ground; it is also called collapsed cabbage. Its shape is like a basin, spread flat on the ground, not exceeding an inch in height. Its vegetable veins are very wrinkled, like folds, and the color is deep green. Once exposed to heavy frost, its taste is as sweet as licking sugar. It is best cooked and eaten, and is not available anywhere else.

(3) Spinach: Originally named Bolingcai, spinach is also a commonly used vegetable. It originally came from the country of Boling in the Western Regions. Its seeds first entered China during the Tang Dynasty. The leaves are alternate, slightly triangular and pointed, the stem is about five inches high, the flowers are small and yellowish-green, single-sexed, and dioecious. The root is a beautiful red color, and people jokingly call it "red-mouthed green parrot." Once exposed to heavy frost, its taste becomes even sweeter. It is an essential vegetable to serve with raw fish, so its sales are even more widespread in winter.

(4) Luohan Vegetable: Also known as Elan vegetable, it is an annual plant that grows in wet fields. The stem is less than a foot long, the leaves are long and oval, and the reticulated leaves grow in clusters, often up to more than a hundred petals, with the leaf base clasping the stem. In the spring and summer, it blooms with small white flowers, and the fruit is round and small, resembling a round fan shape. Luohan vegetables were previously only available in the countryside of Jiading. There were no such products locally, but recently they have also been sold in baskets in the market. It is best to pick and eat them in winter. After they have bloomed and fruited, the stems and leaves become coarse and old, and are no longer suitable for eating. The vegetable has a spicy and fragrant aroma. In lean years, people pick its stems and leaves and pickle them to make pickles, mix them with green fruit, and pack them in bottles to give to distant guests. Its taste is fragrant, sweet, and delicious. Those with a fondness for wine especially cherish it as a top-grade item.

Another Column: Investiture of the Gods and the Biography of the Five Hegemons and Seven Powers

— Hen Shui

Regarding Mr. Ren of Yanqiao Village's research on the Investiture of the Gods, I, the younger brother, have some slight views and dare to offer them for correction. Chinese chapter novels, such as Water Margin, Romance of the Three Kingdoms, and Journey to the West, have all undergone several evolutions. What is popular in society today is not their original appearance. Investiture of the Gods is one of the four great classic novels, and is no exception. As far as we know now, Investiture of the Gods seems to have originated from King Wu's conquest of Zhou. However, it does not directly inherit from it. In between, there is still a Biography of the Five Hegemons and Seven Powers. I, the younger brother, have a Qianlong edition of this book, half of which is already blurred, but the general idea can be discerned. Several sections in its first volume (ancient chapter novels have sections that are not divided into chapters; the details will be discussed separately another day) all record Jiang Ziya's assistance to Zhou in destroying Zhou, about 20,000 to 30,000 words, with no mention of Investiture of the Gods. The book has a preface by Chen Meigong. Even if it is a forgery, it must have been produced at the same time. Chen was a famous scholar with great fame in the late Ming Dynasty, while the Qing people despised and ridiculed him and would not bother to forge it. This book also has a Ming edition, with very good illustrations, now in the collection of the Peking University Research Institute Library. The book refers to the Ming Dynasty as the "Imperial Dynasty," which is conclusive evidence that it was written in the Ming Dynasty, not the Yuan Dynasty. Perhaps, the Book of King Wu's Conquest of Zhou was cut and placed at the beginning of this chapter? I, the younger brother, have not seen the Book of King Wu's Conquest of Zhou, and dare not make a definite statement. As for whether the author of Investiture of the Gods is Xu Zhonglin, it is indeed questionable, but at least this person is the reviser, like Jin Shengtan in the seventy-first chapter of Water Margin. As Mr. Ren of the village said, Xu's name is not printed at the beginning of the volume, but in the second volume. The copy I have also has the same, and I do not know the reason. Also, the characters in this book are the same as the characters in Journey to the West, such as Nezha, Yang Jian, and Cihang Daoren and Guanyin, and so on. Upon careful examination, it seems that they each have their own origins, but they have also taken stories from each other and expanded on their theories. I, the younger brother, read the Ming Dynasty's "Casual Notes from Jie'an," and learned that Journey to the West has a script for singing. Therefore, there must be many mythical novels from the Ming Dynasty that have now been lost. It is possible that Journey to the West and Investiture of the Gods have another source, which has already been lost. Now, I will tentatively propose a lineage chart of Journey to the West and Investiture of the Gods, and hope to receive corrections from experts!

Song Dynasty's Poetry of Tang Sanzang's Journey to the West → Script for Singing Four Journeys → Four Journeys → Wu's Journey to the West → Xu's Investiture of the Gods → Yuan Dynasty's King Wu's Conquest of Zhou → Biography of the Five Hegemons and Seven Powers → Creation Evolution → Romance of the Seven Kingdoms

Records of Fleeting Fragrances from the Imperial Incense

— Original by Princess Der Ling, translated by Qin S.O.

Can she still be optimistic when she thinks about these things? Thinking about it later, her brain nerves were obviously completely surrounded by shadows of sorrow, pain, disappointment, depression, and so on. No wonder everyone in our palace was trembling with fear, and anxiously and cautiously restraining ourselves! On this day, I actually managed to squeeze out some free time. I took advantage of this opportunity to rush to the ancient palace where Emperor Tongzhi's relics were stored. My intention was to see if the small clay rabbit with eyes and a tongue that could turn on its own, which the Empress Dowager had personally taken there a few days ago, had been returned to its original place. I searched for a long time, but could not find any trace of it. Of course, the Empress Dowager had carefully collected this treasure of Tongzhi. Presumably, when we are not with her, she cannot help but take it out to look at and caress!

I don't know how this day passed. Later, the night finally arrived. The heavy atmosphere of melancholy that enveloped this entire ancient palace during the day now felt even deeper and thicker! The sky seemed to be lower than usual, and people felt more difficulty breathing. What's more, a very coincidental thing happened, as if Heaven was deliberately trying to intimidate the Empress Dowager, making her wholeheartedly believe in the predictions of the two astronomers: a sudden north wind rose violently outside the palace, howling and shaking the windows, making them rattle. As dinner time approached, my service time was up, and my spirit and body both felt tired. I said goodbye to the Empress Dowager and hurried out, first leaning against the railing on a long corridor in front of our bedroom, planning to take a breath of fresh air. Unexpectedly, the purple and white lilacs were blown wildly in the air by the wind, and therefore all the unpleasant odor they possessed felt even stronger, and even made me think of the smell of death! Financial Bulls Emerge, Gold Price Drops Again by $7.40

Lowest Price $932.80

Large Shorts Take Advantage of Low Prices to Cover, Quite a Few to Beijing

Yesterday, large bullish forces emerged in the gold market, selling pressure was dense, the entire market broke through the $40 mark again, and the drop was quite severe. Large short positions took advantage of the low prices to cover, temporarily maintaining the situation. The market outlook is still weak, but the overall trend has stabilized slightly. In the early morning, overseas silver markets were flat, exchange rates fluctuated slightly, and London spot gold rose by one penny. Off-market pre-market trading opened at $43.40, but unexpectedly, there were quite a few people who took the opportunity to sell off. The chips were originally loose, lacking support, and large traders also came to supply the market, gradually falling. The Central Bank's official exchange rate announcement showed that the British and American currencies were flat, and the customs gold unit rose by 0.02%. The standard gold price was posted at $965.60, slightly lower than before. After the opening, the banks had a slight appetite for buying, and the sentiment was still flat. There was still a strong desire to buy at low prices, which allowed the price to rebound. However, large traders took advantage of the high prices to sell aggressively, and the buying side ultimately lacked strength. The $40 mark was broken. Securities

Bond Market Under Strong Manipulation

23 Customs Bonds Rise Another 2.7 Yuan

96 Bonds Drop Alone by 1.0 Yuan

Yesterday at the Chinese Securities Exchange, the 23 Customs Bonds turmoil still hadn't subsided. Market changes were unusually intense, quite different from ordinary fluctuations, full of unpredictable twists and turns, and capable of the most extreme ups and downs. At the same time, the 96 Public Bonds, in the absence of rumors or ordinary conditions, unexpectedly experienced a sharp decline. Other various forms gradually shifted from low to high. The chaotic state of the market was truly rare. According to market rumors, there was still a plan to recall the 23 Customs Bonds and reissue the 24 Customs Bonds. The market frantically pushed up and suppressed prices, causing a city-wide uproar. Transactions were unusually robust. On one side, long positions flooded the market, causing a very sharp drop. On the other side, short positions were covered and prices were raised, resulting in a violent surge. Before the government has announced a formal plan, violent fluctuations are likely unavoidable. If the facts are the opposite, then a sharp advance will be followed by a rapid retreat, and a crazy decline may also be expected. Because the number of general trend-following buyers is already significant, once the line is shaken, the rush to sell will also be alarming. An investigation of the various bonds issued by the government reveals that all procedures for principal and interest payments have been reviewed and approved by the Legislative Yuan and have the nature of law. Their nature is the same as that they cannot be arbitrarily prepaid and cannot be repaid past the due date. If there is organized monopolistic trading, then the current market price is actually only about six yuan away from the face value, and it will soon be difficult to avoid a sell-off. However, the 96 Bonds have fallen for two consecutive days, a small drop of one or two yuan, which is also an unexpected move. Yesterday's events were as follows: at the opening, bond prices mostly continued to rise by small amounts of two, three, or four jiao. The 20 Customs Bonds rose by three and a half jiao due to the excessive drop the day before. The 23 Customs Bonds, starting at an initial market price of 78.50 yuan at the beginning of this month, rose another 1.5 yuan compared to the closing price the day before, reaching a maximum of eight jiao. At that time, numbers 4, 11, and 46, etc., were sold, and each group's selling pressure was very strong, plummeting to 7.2 jiao at the close. This was the trend from high to low for this month's term. When the March term opened, people's hearts turned weak, and selling pressure was extremely strong, opening at 75 yuan, a sharp drop of two yuan compared to the closing price the day before. At that time, numbers 49 (probably representing 32), 69, and 74, etc., suddenly appeared on the market, aggressively absorbing and bravely raising prices, gradually rising, and the trading was unusually lively. The rise to 78 yuan at the close of the session was inevitably criticized as manipulation. The next session opened around 4:00 PM, and bond markets mostly rebounded by one or two jiao to four or five jiao. The 23 Customs Bonds rebounded again, surging 2.7 jiao. However, number 32 had a lot of selling. Opening a position and closing it in the next session does not escape the nature of speculation. Judging from yesterday's trend, the monopolistic situation already has cracks, and those who cannot afford to receive the goods or do not have goods to deliver should not try it lightly. As a result of the market price, the 23 Customs Bonds surged about 2.7 yuan, the Complete Six rose nearly one yuan, and the 96 Bonds fell sharply again by eight jiao to one yuan. Other varieties rose and fell equally, about three or four jiao up and down. The total number of transactions was 19.91 million yuan, of which the 23 Customs Bonds accounted for 6.615 million yuan. Market prices eased further. The outbound traffic was slow, not unlike the pre-holiday atmosphere. (According to the 12th, it was Lincoln's birthday, and the American cotton market was closed.) The textile industry was extremely sluggish, and market prices were nominal. The closing price was stable, with spot prices falling by five pounds and futures falling by four to six pounds. The British cotton market was weak, with spot prices falling by three points and futures falling by one to three points. Indian cotton was initially weak due to bulls closing their positions, but later recovered due to purchases by European exporters. Pingle fell 4.5 Robi, Aumra fell 3 Robi, and Bailuoxi fell 2.5 Robi. Good Spot Sales of Grain Drive 期粉 (Wheat Flour Futures)

Yesterday in the wheat flour market, after the opening in the morning, each month showed signs of initial weakness followed by rising prices. The price quoted for foreign wheat from Chicago fell by about three to four jiao, and Canadian prices fell by about one jiao and six to seven fen. When the opening price was quoted, the near and distant term sentiment was slightly agitated due to the small quotation of foreign wheat. Each month fell slightly by about half a fen. After the second session, actual sales merchants, such as Tianjin and Yingkou merchants, were still diligent in purchasing spot flour. There were frequent purchases. It was heard that 120,000 to 30,000 packages had been traded within two days, and some manufacturers had reduced their vehicle departures, so the need for spot flour seemed more robust. Therefore, this month's contract weakened and then recovered. Factory sales of distant term contracts have decreased, but there are concerns about the continued settlement of foreign wheat, and buying sentiment is not strong. In the current situation, with spot flour sales still active, the distant term contracts will be in a reversed market due to the relationship with foreign wheat. As a result, this month's contract rose by 1.25 fen, the March contract rose by 7.5 fen, the April, May, and June contracts did not move, and the July contract rose by 2.5 fen.

Manufacturers Have No Intention of Receiving 期麥 (Wheat Futures)

Yesterday in the wheat futures market, after the opening in the morning, each month showed signs of weakening and falling prices. The price quoted for foreign wheat from Chicago fell by three to four jiao, and Canadian prices fell by one jiao and six to seven fen. Although the weather was very cold in early spring, the clear sunlight was strong, and no more spring snow was expected. Therefore, at the time of the opening price, the hearts of the contracts all appeared weak. This month's contracts were more volatile due to the manufacturers having no intention of receiving goods. The trading volume for distant contracts was small, with only one to three fen of fluctuation. When the afternoon session opened, this month's contracts were boosted by the active flour market, improving one or two fen. As for distant contracts, the exchange rate was gradually lengthening, spot foreign wheat was not expensive, Australian wheat was quoted at eight jiao and seven fen, and A wheat was quoted at about six jiao. Therefore, people's hearts were still calm. As a result, this month's contract fell by three fen, the March contract fell by two fen, and the April contract fell by one fen. Spot wheat was not purchased by factories and there were no deliveries.

河下 Rice Market: Equal Arrival and Sales

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the origin of various merchants was still sparse, with only fifteen or sixteen boats arriving (a total of over 3,000 shih of goods). The sales market also suddenly turned slack. The overall situation seemed to be balanced. The prices of all thick japonica rice did not change. Although the Qingdao merchants made some movements in late rice, the quantity was only over 300 packages, and there were no ups or downs. Du Yangjian rice remained stable. Yinbianyuan rice was in a stagnant situation.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, the boats from various merchants in Hexia were numbered 21 and 22. The market appetite was slack. The prices of upper, middle, and northern japonica rice fell slightly by a jiao, while the price of Jiashan early rice and northern japonica rice of small price fell by a small number of fen. The prices of Du Jian, Ke Jian, etc. were stable. The prices of other varieties were soft. The arrival of high-quality, thin rice was scarce, the sales were active, and the price was high by one or two jiao.

The manager is Liu Qinxuan. The address is Yanghang Street in the French Concession. It will officially open soon.

Guangbang Sugar Stores Change Silver Term

Changed to Sunday to Pay Silver

Guangbang stores, who also operate branches of longan, are divided into two branches: Provincial City and Hong Kong. All goods sold to merchants are subject to payment terms. The payment term for Provincial City merchants is one month. For example, goods sold from the 1st to the 15th of this month must be paid for on the 14th and 15th of the following month, and those sold from the 16th to the end of the month will be paid for at the end of the following month. The silver term for Hong Kong merchants is shorter, limited to Sundays. For example, goods sold from Monday to Saturday of this week must be paid for at the end of this week. This year, the silver term for Provincial City merchants, starting in February, will also follow the example of Hong Kong merchants, with silver paid on Sundays.

Thin Transactions of Hardware and Tin

Recent transactions in tin are still not prosperous. The market situation is still bleak. Due to the financial constraints of the Shaoxing merchants, their appetite is very dull. The business in Hangzhou and Tianjin is also not active. The market is decorated only by a kind of miscellaneous tin business, so the number of goods opened is very small. The market is strong on the outside but weak on the inside due to the poor environment. Small baked tin was sold for 178 yuan, Dutch tin for 198 yuan, Fuzu tin for 195 yuan, Zheng soldering tin for 65 yuan, auxiliary soldering tin for 53 yuan, and bucket tin for 190 yuan. Compared to Hongpan, there were only a few gains and losses.

However, there are no sales, and people's hearts are very soft. Therefore, according to market standards, there is a great potential for another decline.

Free Talk

Reminiscences of the Old Lunar New Year

— Tang Tao

After trying my hand at writing on New Year's Day, I put down my pen for over a month. During this month, I've seen many articles, some settling accounts of the past, others hoping for the future, all generally expressing sentiments about the New Year.

I also want to write something, also about the New Year. Though it's already very late, it doesn't matter, since there's still the old Lunar New Year.

If something can be made up for, we usually don't care about being early or late. Losing money playing mahjong during the solar New Year? We think: There's still a Lunar New Year anyway. Failing to meet important guests during the solar New Year? We think: There's still a Lunar New Year anyway. Children not getting lucky money, employees not getting rest? Everyone thinks together: There's still a Lunar New Year anyway.

But the so-called "still a Lunar New Year" finally arrives. Playing cards, visiting, getting money, "having fun," naturally, there's another round of excitement. However, auctions, store closures, downsizing, extended hours, bounced checks; this excitement ultimately falls flat.

When the excitement falls flat, things usually calm down, but that's not necessarily the case in Shanghai. The New Year is, after all, something the petty bourgeoisie "can't bear to part with." We have merchants slaughtering livestock and welcoming the God of Wealth; scholars taking advantage of the holiday to hold elegant gatherings; heroes kicking women while they light firecrackers; onlookers standing by the roadside clapping and cheering. Dog racing tracks, movie theaters, taverns and tea houses, streets and alleys, betting on the favorite, guessing the dice, the New Year's gongs and drums, "Gongxi facai!" (Wishing you wealth!)

Shanghai, during this old Lunar New Year, is bustling.

The Lunar New Year in the countryside, as I remember it, was just as lively.

On the first day, before the east even began to turn white, we had to get up to worship heaven and earth, usually with three cups of tea, four plates of pastries, and four plates of fruit. After bowing, we set off firecrackers to open the door, and the year began like that. Then came the New Year visits, first to the family temple, then to the ancestral hall, and then to the living elders. Everyone, young and old, looked happy.

They were happy because they were still alive. In this era of natural disasters and man-made calamities, any commoner could die at any moment. They had actually survived another year on this difficult and hardship-filled path of life. Not only had they not died themselves, but even others were still alive, so they congratulated each other, hoping that this year would still pass smoothly, and that next year there would still be New Year's Day, they would still meet, and they would still congratulate each other.

Year after year, even if it was hard, they still considered it happiness.

When eating on New Year's Day, we usually used a round table, with the whole family sitting around it, meaning that this could win the family's reunion. They were really afraid of "wandering" and "family ruin."

However, they had such a premonition.

What created this premonition in them was the "wandering" of countless people and the "family ruin" of countless people.

The second and third days were still days for New Year visits, with relatives and friends coming and going, chatting intimately, and exchanging good wishes. This was really their only joy. Although there were many days to be happy throughout the year, what others celebrated together was not necessarily what they wanted to celebrate. Only this New Year was theirs. Gambling without having to avoid officials, stealing leisure without being scolded, everyone felt relaxed, free, and uninhibited.

The special features of the New Year were boat lanterns, horse lanterns, dragon lanterns, monks' plays, and flower drum performances, with drumming and singing, continuing until the end of the month.

The Lunar New Year in the countryside, as I remember it, was also bustling.

However, my memory was finally shattered. After this drought, the elders who received New Year greetings from their children and grandchildren last year are now nowhere to be found; the sons who paid New Year greetings to their fathers last year are now sold to nowhere; only a few starving bellies remain, struggling and crying out.

The New Year has arrived again, desolate, lonely, barren, the New Year is no longer theirs. Heavens, who can put on a smile again?

High Altitude (2)

— by Henri Barbusse, translated by Di Zhou

|| On the pale face of Musset, the beard was not so much silver-white as gold-white. Most of the assistants, at this time, had sad faces. The patient, placing his thin hands on the armrests of the easy chair, seemed as if he were on a throne.

Wealthy, idle, seducing women, all for the sake of self-devotion, regardless of his noble, keen sensibility, is often the most cruel beast. And regardless of his true spirit, he is the most lying man.

Now, he is aware of dying. With this supreme, nightly, gentle, melancholy voice, he is murmuring about something. It is this warm voice that causes distress to most hearts.

|| I am satisfied and happy, he says.

|| I have no wishes. I have nothing...

But his eyes were meeting the face of a woman standing there. He stopped talking. It was the face of a young woman he had never seen before, from the side of a relative. This face, trembling with inner emotion, gazed at him.

Desire? Perhaps. Or perhaps the remorse of desire. These are the same thing. Between the conflict and alternation of desire and remorse, there is an unbreakable chain linking them. Now, from his point of view, a new, living thing has appeared. The dream of love for this woman is burning strongly, strongly, inside his decaying body. But now, he has no way to touch this woman's hand. He has fallen into infinite pain. Infinite, that is the infinite sinking to the deepest bottom. And the fishing line that opens the curtain of this dream has fallen on his coffin. His heart, which had already stopped throbbing, became sad and excited again.

Before long, a short time passed. Like a wounded bird falling silently, he quickly weakened. After the people left, when only he and I remained, he said to me:

|| I made a will before, giving you the property. Afterwards, everyone forced me to write other wills. It is in this drawer. Take it and destroy it. I only regret the original will.

|| That won't do...

|| Won't do?

The dying man raised his marble-like forehead, his solemn profile drooping, and with beautiful, bright eyes, fixed on me motionlessly. He stared at me as motionlessly as if he were seeing a strange beast.

|| Follow my will. Don't give it to those people. Give it to you.

I could no longer say "no," and lowered my head powerlessly, my body motionless.

Time passed. People came in again. But the time was already late.

...I said to myself. How foolish is what I have done. Without thinking, I entered a mountain of treasure, and passed by without visiting. It is not I, relying on the edge of poverty, who did the useless thing of recovering the property. What a foolish thing.

In this way, contact with the vast space created a second nature within me. But my heart had no desire to continue to be more advanced than that kind of habit. I have fully invaded the upper levels of the world and passed by. The habit of inverting the old angles of observing things, took away from me, the throbbing of desire, all evil, even the etiquette born of strong selfishness, have disappeared completely from my sight.

He lost the power of understanding. His face was slightly moved by the enormous distress. ... Only sensitive to carnal desires, he who awoke several times, he was dying slowly, slowly.

Dad is Unemployed

— H

Thoughts on Reading "Eternal Labor, Eternal Ease"

— Xian He

Lately, because I myself am feeling the panic of unemployment, I am particularly fond of reading articles discussing unemployment. A few days ago, I read Mr. Wang Pingling's "Eternal Labor, Eternal Ease" in this publication, and I have some small thoughts, which I will now simply write out, hoping that Mr. Wang will be willing to instruct me.

The central idea of this article is to blame unemployment on "serious mistakes" and "undue good fortune," and these "mistakes" and "good fortune," according to Mr. Wang's meaning, are the "concept" of "eternal labor, eternal ease." If this logic is not wrong, then the unemployed masses can only blame themselves for not being able to find a job. "You are unemployed because you are lazy, not capable enough, and have no talent," Mr. Wang's opinion is exactly this. Therefore, he puts forward "three questions" to ask the unemployed masses to reflect on themselves; whether they can avoid submitting a blank paper for these three test questions. Only those who do not submit a blank paper have the hope of a "trial" for several months, otherwise you will have to be asked to go to the streets to have fun.

However, the fact is completely contrary to this theory. If you examine the ranks of the unemployed, there are plenty of members with both talent and learning; on the other hand, among those who enjoy high salaries and generous emoluments, there is no lack of incompetent idiots. Those scum who fantasize about eternal labor and eternal ease are not worth mentioning and deserve to be attacked, but how should Mr. Wang explain this strange phenomenon of "eternal labor" but not being able to achieve "eternal ease," or "eternal ease" but not having "eternal labor"?

The example Mr. Wang gives is university students. He says that "some people think that they are only allowed to endure hardship once, and after obtaining a diploma, they can enjoy it for the rest of their lives," which is of course an appropriate argument, but in fact, there are many university students who have not even obtained a "day and night" of trial, let alone "for the rest of their lives." How can Mr. Wang explain the fact that "graduation is unemployment"?

As for Mr. Wang's claim of one or two years of ability, one or two years of survival rights, this statement is also a bit abstract and mysterious, isn't it?

I think that if correcting a few wrong ideas can solve "part" of the unemployment problem, then Mr. Wang's statement at the beginning of the article that "I don't know how many organizations have been established to solve this problem, I don't know how many government orders have been changed to solve this problem, and I don't know how many celebrities and scholars have racked their brains to solve this problem" is simply incredible.

In fact, Mr. Wang himself also admits that this is a "difficult to solve" "social problem"!

Zhong Wu (Part 1)

— Ouyang Shan

Liang Yun, who watched over the lumber in the Guang Sheng Fa Lumberyard, was a man almost fifty years old. He was short, but very robust – and in that narrow exterior was hidden a heart that was broad and honest. He had no children; he had married a wife when he was young, but she ran away after a few years. Afterwards, he lived alone, conscientiously fulfilling his responsibilities in his job, without any desires. When his wife abandoned him, he was still working as a clerk in a mountain goods store in Qinzhou that specialized in collecting wild game such as white deer, golden pheasant, and pangolins. Knowing that this would become an irreparable shame for him, he hid in a dark room and cried sadly – afterwards, he left that small city embraced by desolate mountains and the sea, working as a stoker on a steamboat, a blacksmith in a fish market, until he arrived in Guangzhou, never mentioning that he had once had a woman.

His character was tranquil, to the extent that he resembled a plain tile placed in a brazier of red-hot coals; it could roast a plucked hen, but it would never ignite itself. Sometimes he caught a wild dog, secretly killed it, and cooked its meat with so many sauces that the rich aroma could be smelled from twenty feet away. Then he would call many friends to eat, saying how much money he had spent on this food, and happily listened to the reactions of those people to this little lie – praise or ridicule. There was no choice of goodwill or malice, as if he had never used his will to force others, and his own lies did not harbor any ambition.

Zhong Wu, a burly, generous "ownerless wandering spirit" who often spoke exaggeratedly, boasting about his ability to make fools of policemen, small merchants, and landlords, and who had a shoulder injury, was staying in his small wooden hut. When the bone injury on his shoulder was slightly better, he completely forgot Liang Yun's advice. He had urged him to hide in the wooden bunk in the hut during the day, so that the storage department director would not find out that there was a stranger staying in the lumberyard, but Zhong Wu ran around with his chest out, sometimes even standing at the gate and scolding the coolies carrying wood, making others think for a moment that he was the newly appointed director.

Seeing Liang Yun's flustered expression when someone walked over from the distant riverbank whistling, Zhong Wu said:

"Isn't the director's name Jin Yao? – Fatty Hu Shou told me. What reason would a character named Jin have! He might want to hire me to work in the storage department – at least, he should know that I am useful when someone comes to steal wood." Or, rubbing his injured chest with one hand, he cunningly said: "These people, even including the boss of Guang Sheng Fa, are not golden-eyed white-browed tigers, they are just bedbugs – let them have a blood bead, and they will never bite to death. Once last year; a bunch of brothers forced me like a hunt, and I had no choice but to jump into a canal, walking half a mile underwater – later, while I was sunbathing on the embankment, I accidentally caught a bedbug – it seemed to have put on a brand new suit, coffee-colored, emitting a sparkling light. I really had never encountered a better-looking bedbug, so I immediately regarded it as a friend in need, and loved it tenderly. I put it on my arm, wanting to see with my own eyes how it sucked my blood – at that time, it really had nothing annoying about it, it didn't dare to be presumptuous at all, its gentleness and compliance simply moved me very much. I stretched out a finger to tease it, blowing it upside down with a gentle breath, and finally carefully found a safe corner in my pocket for it and put it there. After doing such a thing, the suffering of that day was almost forgotten, and my heart was much lighter!"

When Liang Yun curled up his nose and laughed like an old monkey, he added:

"So, if the one named Jin really comes, let me negotiate with him – he might still remember the smell in my pocket."

Liang Yun didn't like the exaggerated personality, but he could tolerate it. When Zhong Wu said that he wouldn't be awkward when speaking in front of those people, and that he would speak more fluently and richly than them, making it difficult for them to cope, he always nodded in deep conviction, smiling very kindly.

Zhong Wu's soul was even more burly than his body. He arrogantly trampled over lands with various different colors and smells, using force to make the things around him bow to him, and pointed his teeth at the weakest parts of all creatures. He would not use those necessary base and filthy tricks – to compensate for this shortcoming, he had to tell everyone plainly that his brutal claws were merciless.

Another feature of his character was a good use of humorous metaphors.

"You wander around in the counties of Bao'an and Dongguan, how do you tell people what your purpose is?"

Liang Yun would ask him this when they squatted beside the woodpile sunbathing. And when he answered, his face looked very broad, as if it made his heart feel a lot of gratitude.

"It depends on who it is. Sometimes I say," this is none of your business, brother," you see, there are such people in the world! Kicking me into the mud without telling me why; when I crawl in the mud, they come to question me again. You, don't say anything to them! …"

"But there are also honest people, who really ask you like a friend."

"I'll lie to him. I say I have a younger sister who was abducted, and no matter where I run, I have to find her before I give up. Then everyone cares about me, and some people even become good friends with me because of this. Actually –"

"You don't seem to think of her."

"No, she must also be happy to see me – but there is no reason that can make me have to dig her out of somewhere. It's unnecessary. She should break into her own world, or be sold to Singapore, or… In short, everywhere is vast and boundless."

Zhong Wu narrated some of his own unfortunate experiences in this way, as if they were just some bluffs, which, when he noticed them, could only make him laugh, and despise and feel more at ease.
