Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

The Pessimism of the Commercial Market

— Chui

According to investigations and statistics from banking circles here, the number of large and small shops that have closed down from December 11th to the 8th of this month is very large, and the commercial future is really unthinkable.

Indeed, in recent years, the sluggishness of the commercial market has been getting worse year by year, with a downward trend, and it is not because shops have closed down that we know the decline of the market. The closure of shops only represents the bankruptcy of a part of the commerce, and there are still many shops that want to close but cannot, and want to go bankrupt but cannot, I do not know how many. But the reason why the commercial market has been so sluggish lately is the result of the decline of the entire economic source of our country.

Looking at recent years, extravagance has increased daily, the countryside has gone bankrupt, there have been floods and droughts, production has lagged behind, and foreign capitalism has invaded and exploited. With these various reasons, the people have hardly any room to survive, and various enterprises have no hope of prosperity. The Shanghai market, which seems to be still prosperous on the surface, is also a reflection of the economic bankruptcy of the whole country, because the various situations in the interior are sluggish, and all the economy is concentrated in the city, so this kind of urban prosperity is actually a strong outsider and a weak insider, a fleeting scene, really like duckweed on the water, without any roots.

Taking the commercial side of Shanghai as an example, a large restaurant on the Great Horse Road, which is known as the commercial center, has been doing fairly well in its daily business, but according to people in the restaurant, it is losing money every day and cannot maintain it. I asked how much the rent was? The answer was three thousand five hundred taels. If we add the rent tax and electricity, it cannot be less than four thousand taels. In this way, excluding the capital interest rate, the daily rent and other expenses are not less than two hundred yuan. So if you do not make seven or eight hundred yuan a day, you cannot pay the expenses. May I ask how it is possible for a restaurant to do seven or eight hundred yuan of business every day in this sluggish situation.

Looking at this one family, the rest can be imagined. All kinds of trade cannot be developed, and housing expenses cannot be maintained. Even if the business situation is barely satisfactory, and the income can cover the expenses and pay the rent, it is already a fortunate thing. However, in this time when the business situation is getting worse year by year, the land price is getting higher year by year, and the rent is still expensive. This kind of deformed development is enough to promote the rapid collapse of the market. Regardless of the sluggishness of the commercial situation in recent years, even if the economy is good, it is only doing business for a few landlords. Therefore, the reason why tall buildings are being built everywhere, but no one cares about them, can also be inferred.

After Losing One's Way

— Mo Yan

"A new emperor, a new courtier," I didn't expect things to change so quickly! We finally all encountered an irreparable misfortune. So we handed over our careers to others and scattered like birds and beasts!

Old Lou and I didn't feel too much sadness about this unemployment, because a chicken rib life will always have a day to be abandoned, but the authorities' disposition—the disposition of planting parties and operating private interests—and the homelessness of a group of colleagues, made people feel endless resentment and sympathy.

Although I was constantly shouting to get out of that ghostly place, but now that I have no home to return to, I can't help but think that the past was better than today. Now what can I do? Where am I going? I look at the future with dismay, and I can't help but feel that I have nowhere to turn!

I blindly went to the city twice, and as a result, my hope turned to ashes. All that was in front of me was a dead end! I don't know who is playing with me, I really want to cry! I can only blame myself for not having any skills in life and perseverance in hard work. When King Xiang of Chu was defeated at Wujiang Estuary, he still had a sharp blade to end his life. This time, I can't even find a tool to commit suicide. Otherwise, when I am in a bad mood, I can still destroy myself at will, saving countless times of anxiety and hesitation!

In the inn, Old Lou finally decided to come up with a way out of no way. After a serious and thorough consideration, I felt that if this is also a way to guarantee future life, then there will be absolutely no people in the world who are shouting hungry all day long. I understand that Old Lou's plan is really out of his painstaking efforts to comfort me and himself. People are encouraging me and comforting me, should I have the courage to disagree and refuse in an inhumane way? This is how we decided on our goal.

"We have to get some money to go to the city, the city has our new hope, new life, and everything else!" This is Old Lou's plan.

But I didn't encounter a smooth and convenient problem to solve from east to west, as if the journey I was taking was always rugged and dangerous; in normal times, it was often easy to ask friends for some money, it was nothing, but now, when I was in urgent need, I was at a loss! The biggest reason for this, of course, must be attributed to the year-end, which is cursed by the poor.

People are not like human beings, running around all day, and their food, clothing, and housing have broken the routine. However, the unexpected is still a futile trek, with nothing to gain! To sum up, our poor friends are of course unable to help or have the will but not the power; friends who are slightly wealthy or have a little savings—I don't have any wealthy friends—either say that they have been financially strapped recently, or that the year-end is coming and they are unable to turn around. The words are a sentence that can be concluded: there are really few friends who can be relied on in times of need.

Old Lou's turban spirit is too heavy after all. In the silence of being speechless to each other, he suddenly extemporized two sentences, but they deeply touched the strings of my heart: "It is lamentable that the world is as indifferent as water, how many Guan Zhong and Bao Shu are there in ancient and modern times"!

Finally, with a feeling of disappointment, I ran to a friend who I was embarrassed to ask for help again. His sympathetic face and extremely sincere expression made people feel so moved that they couldn't bear to speak. He is frugal and saves on food and clothing to help friends who are poor, can I still be cruel to ask for it? However, my friend, a friend who makes people prostrate themselves! He discerned my intention and acted as a matchmaker for me, entrusting the heavens to bless me and finding a sum of money that was enough to help me out. After being ashamed, I actually got my wish, and I was not without pleasure in my heart, although the deadline was very close.

Like a fish getting water, I turned my head and went back to tell Old Lou this good news.

The two of us laughed and clapped our hands for a while, and together we carried our suitcases and rushed into the city.

Page 20

A FAT MAN

— Bai She

Cold Evening

I walked along many deserted streets to find a bathhouse. Finally, I found a place called "Something Spring" in an alley. As soon as I entered, the hot, cheap bathhouse air rushed into my nostrils. With the enthusiastic greetings of the attendant, I finally stepped into the warm waiting room, which was seven copper coins more expensive than the one across the street. The humid air was comparable to the heating system in a grand building, making me immediately take off my coat, leaving only the clothes I wore in summer. The attendant poured me a cup of weak tea, and I took out the newspaper I had brought in my pocket to read. In this brief moment, I forgot about the thinness of my clothes and the cold I had felt wandering the streets during the day. I even lit a weak-flavored cigarette, as if I had gathered all the things I could find to put my mind at ease. Even though this place was a smelly warm spring, it was, after all, a place without cold. Just as I was about to finish this weak-flavored cigarette, an unexpected event occurred.

Amidst the attendant's call for "hand towels," I saw a fat man sit down next to me. Because I was leaning back, I only saw the fat man's back. Two creases had formed on the back of his head. Everyone knew that these weren't indentations. Legend has it that a person's brain weighs nine catties and eight taels, but in the fat man's case, it undoubtedly broke the record. However, his shoulders were not much wider than those of an average person, but they grew increasingly large towards the bottom. I have never entered the Louvre Museum, which is filled with famous paintings, and don't know how many layers of human figures are depicted there, but I can guess that if a Cubist painter were to paint a half-body portrait of the fat man, they would use a cone to create it. However, the head at the apex of the cone would be a wooden fish from a Buddhist temple. The attendant used a steaming hot towel to wipe him from his back to his chest. When he wiped the fat man's lower body, the fat man leaned back, and I saw his breasts. The peaks of his breasts were high and erect, just like those of a woman who had given birth, able to tremble from the vibrations of the surrounding flesh. The attendant wrapped his feet with large towels, one at a time. The fat man let him do as he pleased. His legs, which were thicker than the bodies of two children, rested on the attendant's shoulders. After carefully covering the fat man's belly and legs with towels, a foot massager began to massage his thick, short toes. Then, an exceptionally loud snore erupted from the fat man's nostrils, drawing the attention of everyone in the room. I really couldn't stand the squealing of that pig nose, so I went to the bathroom to wash.

After spending half an hour in the bathroom, my lungs could no longer withstand the pressure of the steam. When I returned to my seat, the fat man was still fast asleep, and all I could hear was his snoring. At this time, one of his legs was twitching violently, and the towel covering his lower body had slipped off at some point. The twitching of his leg encroached on my seat, but slapping his leg did nothing. Then, I thought of the nickname that foreigners gave us: "Sleeping Lion." At the same time, I also thought of elephants. Elephants are the largest and fattest of all beasts, but they fear a small mouse crawling into their trunk.

I left the bathhouse close to ten o'clock. The fat man was still asleep and showed no signs of moving. I didn't want to look back at him again, so I walked out.

A Century Apart (Seen in Front of the Paramount Ballroom)

— Wang Yun

In a Sampan

— Hua Zhi

Continuing the Chronicle of a Certain Year

The soldiers only seemed to be invading, not retreating. With the trains cut off, this small town felt like a besieged and isolated city. Although the news from those old, gray insects (spies) was all about victories, in the nights when the wind was strong, I could faintly hear the rumble of cannons.

The shops in the town were all closed. The produce from the fields around the town had all been sold to the army. It seemed that the war at the front would not end in the short term. The food problem for the ten to twenty thousand people inside and outside the town was becoming dangerous. Moreover, so many soldiers had to rely on this town for their food? Li Ma was constantly nagging about returning to her hometown. Her small package almost never left her wrist. Although Ah Yun had no home to return to, she also frowned every day, as if resenting me, her young master, for not finding a way to escape this tiger's den sooner.

Three days later, I knew that holding out was not an option. However, my entire family was living in Hangzhou to take care of my father's illness, or they might have moved away because of the war. I didn't know if they would have to detour home. If I left, we wouldn't be able to communicate with each other, and it wouldn't make sense for everyone to worry about each other. I maintained this situation for a week.

The army in our town was gradually becoming restless. It was clear that the front lines were losing. Ah Yun went to the town once and came back saying that the people in the town had all fled, hiring boats to go from the inner river to the sea. Li Ma forced me to leave. On the one hand, I tried my best to comfort them, and on the other hand, I also tidied up a little, preparing to leave immediately if necessary.

There was still no news from my father's side. Then, one day at dawn, there was rapid gunfire from the direction of the train station. It was said that a platoon of enemies had sneaked over. This urgent report shook my forcibly calmed heart. Ah Yun searched along the town river for boats, but those that had been hired to escape this tiger's den did not return. Another portion had been seized by the army to transport rice and military supplies. Finally, at the highest price, we rented a sampan that no one wanted.

Speaking of sampans, every winter a group of them would come to our town from afar. They were all residents from north of the Yangtze River. A boat was their entire property. They were all able to do handicrafts: sugar candies, paper flowers, clay figures. They had everything that children liked. They would always spend the spring here, making good sales before returning home. Although it wasn't spring yet, they had left early because they saw that the situation was not good. The one we hired was run by two old partners. The man was sick, and the New Year's business had been ruined by the war. They had almost sold their property. Now that they had received this good business, the couple, with tear-stained faces, greeted us three customers. But when we climbed into the cabin, a musty, fishy smell made us nauseous. Li Ma was the first to show a bad face, scolding them to set sail, completely betraying their earnest sincerity.

The back of the sampan was blocked with mud and bamboo strips. Their food and lodging took up the rear part of the ten-foot boat. The two boatmen stood at the bow, and the three of us sat cross-legged, occupying the remaining half. The bottom of the boat was narrow, and if we stretched our legs even a little, they would warn us that the boat would capsize. We looked at Li Ma's face, which we had never seen before. Were we secretly laughing that she regretted leaving so hastily?

The three of us kept our faces tight and didn't exchange a word. Only we ourselves knew the bitterness of this situation. Fortunately, we were going downstream, and the boat quickly left the town river. The green treetops on both sides of the river brushed against the boat, and a few spring birds chirped, easing the tension in our hearts.

I asked the boatman, and he said that it would take at least two nights on this uncomfortable boat to reach Shanghai. Since we had reached this point, I took out a cigarette to smoke and pretended that this was a unique trip, admiring the scenery around us.

The river was straight, and the small boat floating in the middle of the river felt as if it was stopped there. I thought that it would be great to float three large cups of wine in the moonlight. But when I looked out at the continuous fields on both sides, my cheerful heart could not imagine it that way. Where had those farmers gone? The soil was turned over, and the mud blocks were cracked like turtle shells in the sun. Why were these hereditary farmers so lazy? There was no wisp of smoke rising from the thatched houses next to the fields. A thin, weak stray dog walked alongside our boat, its hungry red eyes constantly glancing at us!

Then, I closed my eyes, letting the sampan take me further and further away from my hometown—that house that my father, grandfather, and great-grandfather had worked so hard to build!

Morning in Winter

— Wu Fei

Rubbing my sleepy eyes, I walked onto the street. A cold wind blew across my neck, making me shiver. The street was quiet and still, without any noise. Although the wheels of the manure cart were playing the marching song of the dawn, the people in the city were still searching for their sweet dreams in the land of slumber. The surrounding air also seemed to have fallen into a silent zone. I could even hear my own breathing very clearly. Walking onto the bridge, I exhaled a long breath into the air. A stream of misty heat came out of my mouth and dissipated into the space. Looking at the sky, I saw that it was as gray and dim as if a curtain had been stretched over it. Although there were a few clouds slowly moving, their momentum was slower than a sailboat sailing against the wind, almost imperceptible.

"How cold it is! This kind of winter morning is like it's about to snow!" That's right, wasn't this the coldest part of winter? It should be snowing!"

I thought this, keeping my head down and walking silently forward. My toes were moving in a certain direction, but I didn't care. My entire consciousness was immersed in contemplation.

"It's cold! The clothes on the children aren't warm enough. You have to make them a cotton-padded coat!" My wife had called me back and told me these words every time I left the house, suddenly breaking into my heart. "Yes! The children are still only wearing a thin, old garment. It's definitely not warm enough. And my wife herself is only wearing that six-year-old tattered cotton-padded jacket. How can she keep out the cold! I have to find a way to make them a new garment each to get through this winter; but, but where is the money?"

Walking slowly, thinking silently, my footsteps were heavy, and my heart was as still as water.

Finally, the sky gradually brightened, but the winter sun was still hiding in the clouds. The birds on the branches had already been startled by the passersby and had flown away with a "whoosh." I was dragging a long shadow and unintentionally wandered into the park. The withered yellow lawn was covered with a thick, white frost. The blades of grass were weighed down and hanging upside down.

"The frost last night was as thick as snow, no wonder I didn't sleep warmly; besides, that tattered quilt was still the one we made when we got married. Now it's hard and broken, how can it still be warm! Looking at the frost, I couldn't help but think of the cold last night, and at the same time, I also thought of wanting to make a new cotton-padded garment for my wife and children, but where can I get the money? I felt disappointed, I felt pain, "Ah! A man!"

I no longer had the courage to continue thinking about it, but the more I didn't want to think about it, the more the vortex of thoughts tightened in my heart. I walked to the river and heavily threw my body into an outdoor chair, stretching out my legs and lying on it, as if my whole body was paralyzed, without any strength.

Shanghai Shen Bao Local Supplement Automotive Weekly

New Dodge Six-Cylinder Car

— Fu

Value Exceeding Price

The 1935 New Dodge automobile. It is so exquisite and magnificent, its style so beautiful, and its quality so outstanding, that experts unanimously assumed its price must be high. No one believed its selling price could be so low.

One hundred and seventy-five discerning evaluation experts guessed the selling price of the New Dodge car. The results showed that all guesses were higher than the actual price. Some even guessed $200 to $300 more than the actual price. It is not surprising that these individuals did not guess correctly. Yet, their accuracy is still worthy of experts and is truly admirable. This is because a vehicle with such a low selling price, such ingenious design, and such robust construction is unprecedented. The New Dodge car has ninety-five fundamental improvements, making it exceptionally comfortable, economical, fast, and safe. The car captivates at first sight, as every part is beautiful and pleasing. Upon personally driving it, one is amazed by its newly invented harmonic management. Driving and handling are extremely smooth and convenient. All major driving actions, such as steering, braking, shifting, and using the clutch, are effortless and at will. Its stability and road-hugging ability during travel surpass any previous automobile. Regardless of road conditions, the New Dodge can speed along smoothly, as if gliding. Even on sharp turns, it remains safe and reliable at high speeds, with no risk of tilting or shaking. These advantages are due to the Dodge engineers' unique secret in evenly distributing weight on all four wheels.

What is especially commendable about the New Dodge is its unparalleled economy. The superior engine is exceptionally quiet. Its absolute reliability is a traditional Dodge feature. It reaches speeds of over eighty-five miles per hour. Gasoline consumption is particularly economical, saving fifteen to twenty cents per dollar spent. Oil consumption is also surprisingly low. In addition, the New Dodge retains all the renowned advantages of Dodge, such as the all-steel safety body, floating engine mounts, and hydraulic brakes.

Some say that the 1935 New Dodge car has so many features, yet its selling price is only slightly higher than that of a small car. Therefore, it is expected that people will be happy to purchase a large car to enjoy the true pleasure of driving.

Current Status of the Japanese Automobile Industry

— Yu

| Exports to Australia |

Although Japan is an industrial country, its heavy industry is far less developed than its small industry. Therefore, the automobile industry in Japan is still very young. Most cars in Japan come from Europe and America, and domestic production is very small. In recent years, the government and industry have paid close attention to automobile manufacturing because, while automobiles are ordinary transportation tools related to industry and commerce, they also play a very important role in military transportation. With the current perilous international situation, the Far East crisis deeply hidden, and powerful nations around the world burying their heads in expanding their military equipment, the Japanese attention to the automobile industry is naturally not an exception.

According to the latest Japanese automobile magazines, the current state of the Japanese automobile industry is roughly as follows. The Japanese automobile manufacturing industry, like other industries, has made significant progress. Automobile manufacturing can be divided into two areas: automobile manufacturing and parts manufacturing. Since last year, the automobile manufacturers that everyone has been longing for have been able to implement their work, greatly increasing efficiency. The emergence of new factories and the expansion of old factories have been reported frequently in newspapers in recent months. Therefore, the general public, especially those with knowledge of automobile manufacturing, are extremely surprised by its rapid progress.

The most noteworthy aspect of the Japanese automobile industry is its rapid progress. Compared to other industries, for every step other industries take, the automobile manufacturing industry takes ten steps. Therefore, its progress is no less than ten times greater. Some may ask, what kind of stimulus has the Japanese automobile manufacturing industry been subjected to that has allowed it to progress so rapidly? This is entirely due to the increase in domestic and foreign markets. In the past, production was simple and sales were sluggish, but now, with the daily advancement of manufacturing methods, it is no wonder that it can spread without needing promotion. Several years ago, the general public always believed that Japanese-made products requiring precise craftsmanship could not be compared with foreign goods. Later, the press broke this stereotype. Now, domestically produced products are indeed popular in the country, and foreign goods have no way to exert their competitiveness.

Despite many obstacles in the environment, Japanese automobile production has increased every year. In the past ten months, domestic supply has exceeded demand. Although manufacturers have been manufacturing with all their might, the result is still insufficient. Several years ago, the foreign small car market had already been caught up by Japanese-made products. Moreover, exports of various Japanese-made automobile engines are increasing day by day, and the quantity is greatly increasing. It is expected that once the factories currently under construction are completed, Japan's automobile exports will have a significant increase.

The reason why the Japanese automobile industry has been able to develop so rapidly is, on the one hand, due to the success of manufacturing technology and the expansion of market sales. On the other hand, it is because the automobile industry itself has not been severely affected by the economic recession. In recent years, the world economic recession has been everywhere. Although some say that signs of recovery have already emerged everywhere, who can say whether prosperity will ultimately come? Japan has naturally also been hit by this economic blow. However, why has the automobile industry been able to jump out of this circle and have unique and satisfying progress? This is naturally because only the automobile industry is new, young, and full of vigor and perseverance, and therefore able to advance rapidly.

Although what is seen in the Japanese market now are mostly automobiles from European and American countries, this phenomenon will not last in the near future. At present, other industries in Japan are able to surpass Europe and America, so the automobile industry will naturally not remain inferior for long. Moreover, the current automobile manufacturing technology has already caught up with Europe and America. The expansion of the automobile market is, of course, expected. Japan's automobile products have made extraordinary progress. Therefore, various parts are not only sold domestically, but are also welcomed and satisfied overseas. They are gradually sold to various parts of the world. This progress has occurred in a short period of time, so the economic recession cannot penetrate the automobile manufacturing industry. Japanese automobiles are now sold to Australia. Parts and chassis are shipped to Melbourne for assembly and undergo various tests by agents.

Although the above is mostly in the tone of the Japanese and may have overstated the facts, after reading it, we can also understand the Japanese perseverance and hard work, which cannot be underestimated. I am afraid that in a few years, her automobile products will be even more numerous.

The Great Plan of the Ford Factory in 1935

— Ying Dai

Spending $415 Million US

Increasing the Number of Employees to 87,000

Spending US$415,000,000 and employing 87,000 workers, with plans to produce one million or more cars throughout the year—this is the grand plan of the Ford factory for 1935. Senior officials, engineers, and statisticians at the Ford main factory spent weeks considering this ambitious plan, with thorough planning on both the production and sales fronts. They decided to spend US$415,000,000 on 6,008 automobile raw material suppliers across the United States in 1935. Under this huge expenditure, the 1,757 suppliers in Michigan alone, all directly related to Detroit, who own factories to manufacture automobile materials, are projected to spend US$300,000,000. Once this mass production plan is implemented, the Ford factory's monthly expenditure in Detroit alone will be US$6,861,000.

Regarding his business, someone recently discussed it with Ford, and he said, "From the perspective of the Ford factory, the recession seems to have passed." "Based on our experience, the past six months," he said, "the facts tell us that in the coming year, the business can progress." "So, in your opinion, has the recession completely passed?" Someone asked Ford. "Why, the recession will soon pass throughout the United States," he replied. "If American industrialists completely forget the spelling of the word 'recession' and continue to promote their businesses with the sound and good business spirit unique to Americans, then they can control the entire United States. Similarly, they can enable all Americans to apply their sound and good common sense."

The promotion of the automobile business will undoubtedly employ many unemployed workers. According to a report from the Ford factory, in the past year, many workers in Detroit and its suburbs have been waiting for the factory to hire more. In recent months, the number of employees hired has reached 55,000 at its peak. Although the number of people employed has decreased due to internal reorganization and planning, as soon as the recovery plan is launched, workers will be hired immediately. When adding workers in the future, the factory has decided to prioritize hiring old Ford factory workers and skilled workers from other Detroit factories. According to the pre-planned figures, if the total number of cars produced in the coming year reaches one million or more, then at least 87,000 workers will be employed.

Of this huge expenditure, as pre-planned, 164,000 vehicles will be used to directly transport raw materials, and 160,000 vehicles will be used to transport goods purchased from overseas after they arrive in the United States. The transportation costs alone, mostly railway transportation costs, will be US$74,000,000. The largest expenditure item on Ford's 1935 budget is the purchase of car bodies, which will be US$100,000,000. This expenditure is almost entirely paid to car body manufacturers in the Detroit area for the purchase of car bodies.

In addition, a significant expenditure is the purchase of steel and non-ferrous metals, totaling US$75,000,000. The steel supplied by Ford's own steel mill is insufficient, and the steel purchased from the open market accounts for US$53,600,000. Malleable pig iron is US$6,618,000, and white iron is US$2,683,000 (not including what is produced in River Rouge). Among the non-ferrous metals, aluminum is the most expensive, accounting for US$6,000,000, followed by bronze at US$3,600,000, lead at US$1,443,000, tin at US$1,151,000, and zinc at US$337,750.

The rubber industry has indeed benefited greatly from the Ford factory, because Ford's 1935 budget shows the purchase of rubber tires at US$22,500,000, and raw rubber at US$6,000,000. It is estimated that another US$32,000,000 will be spent on other raw materials used to assemble car bodies, including US$36,727,000 for fabrics, blankets, leather, and other materials used for sewing and repairing car bodies, US$11,000,000 for glass, US$4,300,000 for paint, and US$3,000,000 for the purchase of wood, including luggage boxes and packaging. The most important item in the budget is the expansion of Ford's current steel mill and the increase in power, requiring a fund of US$14,000,000 for a new factory. In addition, the purchase of Ford factory machinery, equipment, and various items requires an expenditure of US$2,500,000, plus fuel and non-productive labor (such as machine movement and window cleaning), resulting in a total expenditure of US$415,000,000 in the 1935 budget.

Newly Emerging Cast Iron Alloys in Automobile Manufacturing

— Rong Lin

In recent years, the progress of automobile manufacturing has been rapid, and the innovation of its applied materials is also remarkable. Take cast iron alloy as an example, its resistance to melting and rust, and its enhanced strength are better than steel, while the cost is much lower. Among the various materials mixed in the alloy, nickel is the most abundant. It can harmonize the components of the iron, prevent hard particles from forming, avoid disasters caused by uneven thickness, and dissipate heat easily, which is of great benefit. Other materials such as chromium, steel, vanadium, and sand are also added, each with its own use.

Usually, the materials added to cast iron alloy used as cylinder material are 1-1.5% nickel, 0.3-0.5% chromium, and 1.5% silicon. With this composition, when seeking the same mechanical strength as steel, its weight can be reduced by about 15%.

For cast iron alloy used for brake levers, 2.5-3.0% nickel, 1.5-1.8% sand, 0.4-0.6% chromium, 1.0% iron, and 2.8% carbon can be added. The amount can further increase resistance, allowing high-speed vehicles to brake suddenly without danger.

In the United States, rear axles and drive shafts are also mostly made of new alloys, which can obtain stronger bending and pressure resistance. For rear axles, the composition is 3-4% nickel, 1.5% silicon, and 2.5% carbon. For drive shafts, the composition is 1.1% nickel, 0.3-0.35% magnesium, 1.8-2.0% silicon, 0.3-0.25% chromium, and 3% carbon.

The material required for pistons has mostly been aluminum-iron alloy, but because its resistance is too great, its body is too heavy, and it is difficult to dissipate heat, it is difficult to be satisfied. There are also copper-chromium-iron combinations, but they are not very suitable due to their excessive expansion performance. The current progress is that the alloy used for pistons is iron with 1.0-2.0% nickel, 3.5% and 3.0% sand, while the one for valves is 3.8% nickel, 0.8% chromium, 1.0% carbon, 3.0% carbon, and 1.5% silicon. Then, high mechanical efficiency can be obtained, and accumulated heat can also be easily dissipated.

In addition, there are compositions with 0.6% vanadium, 1.5% chromium, and 0.25% carbon, which have a hardness of 850-900 Vickes, and those with 18.0% chromium and 8.0% nickel can be heated to 1000-1500 degrees Fahrenheit without any expansion. These are all advances in modern cast iron alloys.

[Image description: A majestic view of the 1935 Dodge six-cylinder two-door sedan is shown. The new car has arrived in Shanghai and is on display in the showroom of the China Motor Company.]

New Fuel for Automobiles

— Yao

At a meeting of the New York branch of the Society of Automotive Engineers in September of this year, it was predicted that streamlined cars will become popular everywhere in the near future, and their speed will definitely break the record of the current new-style streamlined trains.

The coolant used in this high-speed car is the engine's fuel—butane and propane gas. It is said that using this new fuel doubles the compression ratio compared to using gasoline now, and the weight of the fuel can also be reduced by 20%.

Butane and propane have been used to cool engines in the past. Now, they are used as fuel at the same time. This allows the engine's heat dissipation and fuel consumption to be proportional to the engine speed, so it is most suitable. Moreover, this method does not take up space or increase weight, and there is no difficulty in driving.

The compression ratio of ordinary gasoline engines is roughly around 5:1. If propane is used, the compression ratio can be increased to 10:1. If butane is used, it can be increased to 7:1.

When this fuel passes through the carburetor, it has almost become a gas because it has previously absorbed engine heat. It is extremely easy to mix with air, so combustion in the cylinder can be more complete. Oil consumption can be reduced, and the production of carbon deposits can also be eliminated.

These two new fuels are by-products of kerosene refining. The price is not much different from ordinary gasoline. Because they evaporate very easily, transportation is more difficult, so they are only suitable for commercial use.

With slight modifications, ordinary gasoline car engines can be converted to use this new fuel.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special

The Famous British Novelist Hugh Walpole in Hollywood (Part 2)

— Huang Tianshi

In "David Copperfield," he tried as much as possible to use the original dialogue from Dickens. There is only one scene in the movie that differs from the novel: he had David and Dora meet in a theater, not in David's father's office. David's father died early. The relationship with his late father was already severed. This is suspected to be an error. The original novel needs to be checked. - Editor's Note.

"I believe the film is a very capable work," Walpole reported.

Is the rumor that Charles Laughton withdrew from the film true? Did he give up playing Micawber because he "hated Dickens"?

"Yes, that's true," Walpole replied. "He didn't want to accept the role at first, but he agreed after my persuasion. I originally thought he could show his skills greatly. But he is not suitable for comedic roles, and he is very clear about that himself. He really hates Dickens' works, considering them too childish and too shallow."

What were Walpole's feelings about his first appearance on the screen?

"They asked me to play Vicat. It's a minor role. They filmed my scene in one day. The plot describes me preaching in church when David falls asleep in the audience. Someone spread the news that I was very flustered under the lights. This is not true. I felt completely joyful. Acting in movies is much easier than acting on stage; you won't forget your lines or lose your self-control.

"I hope that in the near future, we can set up a film room in our homes, like a picture room," he said. "There are many great films that we would be very willing to keep and re-watch, like 'The Birth of a Nation,' 'David Copperfield,' 'Little Women,' etc. Of course, only some works have immortal value, but our film room can store a hundred films and can plan a simpler sound projector. If movies truly have eternal value, I guarantee that this kind of development is indispensable. Then, naturally, more producers will devote themselves to making films with lasting value."

Walpole is preparing to return to England immediately and will come to Hollywood again this July to continue film work. Someone asked him if he wanted to write original screenplays, and his answer was "No!"

"The best way is to adapt other people's stories into screenplays," he replied. "You don't have to worry about your story being split up by a producer and completely changing the original meaning. Before I start writing original screenplays, I must first obtain a considerable guarantee that it can be realized according to my ideals. If producers can provide this kind of guarantee, then writers like Shaw, Wells, etc., can be spared the hesitation about writing stories for movies.

"I believe that writers will occupy a more important position in film production; on the one hand, a writer must also understand that he needs to cooperate commercially with the producer, director, and set designer. The most important thing is that all parties trust each other. Many films fail because the staff is not harmonious. Every atom must be absolutely harmonious; this does not mean that we have to be completely obedient; we had fierce debates about 'David Copperfield,' but everyone respected each other's opinions. Only this method can hope to produce a perfect film." (To be continued)

Film Reviews

Review of "Cheating Cheaters"

— You Jing

Cheating Cheaters, shown at the Great Shanghai Theater

This is another detective film emphasizing the suspenseful love relationship between men and women.

Perhaps because it was adapted from a stage play, among the many detective films without structure or plot, "Cheating Cheaters" is considered one of the better ones.

I am ashamed to say that I am not very familiar with the original author, Max Marcin, and it is inconvenient to say much here. Just from what is shown to us on the screen through the lens, I feel that calling Cheating Cheaters, translated as "Working Hard for My Love," a Great and Famous Stage Play is somewhat of an exaggeration.

The plot begins on a ship from Paris to New York. Miss Nen, the daughter of Brokden, falls in love at first sight with the young Tom on the same ship. After arriving in port, she rents a house and becomes his neighbor.

Both families appear to be somewhat unscrupulous at the same time, boasting about their wealth in a sneaky way and carefully investigating where the wealth lies.

Mr. Brok invites Tom's family to dinner, and he disguises his accomplices as servants and Miss Nen's music professor, etc. When the sumptuous banquet is over, a servant sends a blank telegram, falsely claiming that the old couple and servants have gone to Chicago. Miss Nen is left to live in Tom's house to learn music, which deepens their love under the moonlight. In the leisure time after dinner and wine, the two families' properties and secret hiding places are revealed. The drama unfolds in this ambiguous atmosphere, with each family scheming against the other. The playwright and director handle these clues quite delicately and concisely, which is commendable.

The plot unfolds with the two families stealing from each other. Tom and his son are tied up by the Brok family for stealing from them; and the Brok family is similarly threatened by the electricity in the Tom family's vault. Miss Nen secretly summons the police, capturing all seven or eight people from both families, and confiscates all the treasures of both families as stolen goods. At this time, the playwright tells the audience that Miss Nen is actually the detective Alice, and she pretended to be a female thief to create these disputes because she loved Tom. So she both bought a husband and solved two cases at the same time.

Thanks to the playwright's efforts, the convoluted plot is woven together quite skillfully. What I mentioned above as being better than the general detective films without structure and plot refers to this. Of course, what is called "good" here is not just meaningful. What we demand as meaningful things is by no means just bizarre plots and precise structures, but works that are divorced from the reflection and indication of real life.

Director Richard Thorpe's technique is not outstanding. The handling of the first half is still commendable, but the second half simply appears hurried, chaotic, and with no spirit infused into each character. It is only when Nen and Tom first meet that the latter lights a flint to illuminate the ornaments on her arm, in order to show his thieving nature, which is quite profound. The director also used quite a few small tricks in Nen's performance. The points of interest in the personalities and actions of Steve and Tony are also quite good.

Apart from a few foreshadowing settings that are not bad, the editor of the screenplay does not seem to be able to handle this stage play in terms of film art, such as the occasions where more people are contacted at the Brok family's reception and the Ball's living room. They all show a stage flavor. As for the occasions with many people from the unfolding of the case to the police station, they are simply restricted by a very deep stage form. Of course, the director is also responsible for this. However, the scene where Tony teaches Miss Nen to play the piano while discussing theft at the Ball's family is helped by the stage play.

The lead actress, Fay Wray, is very hardworking throughout, and her frowns and smiles imply depth and seriousness, which have the taste of a female detective, but the sassy power is still slightly insufficient. The rest all have an average amount of acting to do, and they all pass smoothly.

Hu Ping Can Make Tear Gas

— Qingyun

In the sound dialogue singing film "The Beginning of Man," directed by Shi Dongshan, Hu Ping plays Wei Heling's "woman," who is a boat girl. Because they rely on ferrying passengers across the river every day for a living.

When Hu Ping gave birth to her second son, because the family was poor and could not afford to raise the child, she had to reluctantly send the child to Mrs. Huang, a wealthy woman who had no children, to raise. When Mrs. Huang sent someone to pick up the child, Hu Ping watched helplessly as her own child was taken away, and could not help but cry deeply from maternal love. Yesterday, "The Beginning of Man" was filming this scene.

After this scene was filmed, Shi Dongshan praised her greatly because she performed very realistically, and someone asked her why so many tears flowed when she performed crying? She smiled and did not answer. The fat Chen Linshu interjected and said: "Don't you know, she can make tear gas!" (Thank you)

Audience Opinions

After Watching "The Red Sheep Heroic Story"

— Wanli

During this Lunar New Year, various theaters are competing to show new films, with a variety of dazzling displays, which gives us movie fans such a great feast for the eyes! The day before yesterday, I also followed the crowded audience to the Carlton to see "The Red Sheep Heroic Story."

"The Red Sheep Heroic Story" begins with a scene of the Jade Palace and the Red Steps, where the supreme emperor receives the greetings of hundreds of officials. This scene is very grand, expressing the past history, and the colors are extremely full. Then Hong Xiuquan and Feng Yunshan appear on the screen to meet the audience. Hong is played by Tian Fang, and Feng is played by Yan Ying. They are handsome and energetic, overflowing from their eyebrows. If we talk about casting, it is very appropriate. Hong and Feng ride horses in the countryside, with nature as the background, and the picture is beautiful and unusual, with the poetic realm of "golden-bridled horses neighing on fragrant grassland."

Tong Yuejuan plays a singing girl, singing in a village shop, singing the song of falling flowers and flying catkins. The bankruptcy of the countryside and the displacement of the common people are all poured out in the clear and mournful singing, with a tear in every word, which would greatly move even those with iron hearts!

Generally, people think that Wang Huchen is baptized by Peking Opera and nurtured in the postures and movements of the art. Once he is on the screen, he inevitably brings some Peking Opera colors. Unexpectedly, things are contrary to expectations. In this film, he plays Wei Changhui, and his expression is just right, and he is completely different from Wang Huchen seen on the stage. This is Wang Huchen's debut work, and it can also be said to be a successful work.

The corruption of officials and the ferocity of yamen runners are often expressed as much as possible in small actions, making people's hair stand on end with anger, which shows the director's painstaking efforts.

The final scene of the Taiping Army uprising, self-immolating village houses, the military song is passionate, majestic and powerful, which is unprecedented in domestic films, and the whole drama ends in an extremely tense atmosphere. Looking at the whole film, it is impeccable, promotes national spirit, and promotes revolutionary consciousness. It is a top-notch work.

Movie Novel

David Copperfield (7)

— Liu Cun

But once, David's aunt and Mr. Dick came to David's house for supper, and all the chaos of the family management was immediately revealed. That day, the cook got drunk, the clams were not cut open, and the clam-opening knife could not be found. Half of a leg of lamb was not baked, and half was still raw. This situation clearly showed that David's marriage to Dora was a mistake. Later, David tried to re-hire the loyal Peggotty to take care of Dora and manage the household affairs. But from beginning to end, there was no mention of being a helpmate. The most that Dora could do well was to dip the pen in the inkwell and dip some ink when David was writing.

But David's love remained unchanged. He continued to love her as if she were his child. Year after year passed, and his tenderness and care for Dora did not diminish at all. One night, Dora was sick. That night, Old Fisher also found David and told him that Em'ly had been found by him. Although Old Fisher still wanted revenge, he thanked God that Em'ly could be found. He also told David that Em'ly had been abandoned by Steerforth in Naples. Before Steerforth left, he told his servant to marry Em'ly.

Em'ly was sad about her life experience, met the wrong person, and was left as a servant, so she wanted to die. Steerforth's servant locked her in an empty room. But she eventually managed to escape. Old Fisher managed to find her. When Em'ly saw Old Fisher, she crawled at his feet and begged him for forgiveness. Old Fisher's love was ultimately great. He hugged Em'ly in his heart, and two lines of old tears could not help but flow down.

Although Em'ly had been found, Old Fisher was worried about another matter. He heard that since Ham lost Em'ly, he had disregarded his own life. Whenever there was a storm at sea and a ship capsized and people drowned, he always rushed to be the first to jump into the sea to rescue people. Therefore, Old Fisher asked David to rush to Yarmouth to tell Ham that Em'ly had been found and to advise him not to stake his life anymore.

When David arrived at Yarmouth, he saw a large group of people gathered on the beach, all talking about one thing in a panic. A broken sailing ship was floating at sea, and a person was standing on the ship struggling for life. David saw from afar that the crowd was holding Ham back, but Ham broke free from the crowd and shouted loudly: "Whoever is about to drown, I will go and save." David ran wildly forward, but before he reached the beach, Ham had already jumped into the turbulent, raging sea, desperately extending his arms and climbing left and right in the rapids, heading towards the object.

Ham swam closer and closer to the person struggling in the water, but with each step forward, he was pushed back by the waves. David shouted loudly on the shore, but Ham could not hear him. He fought against the waves. He overcame one wave after another, and finally the face of the person he wanted to save gradually became visible. He looked closely and it turned out to be Steerforth. Ham shouted wildly, as if he had seen some kind of demon. He raised his fist high, as if about to strike. At this moment, suddenly a big wave, like a green mountain, came crashing down, and the broken ship suddenly collapsed with a bang and sank under the waves. Then Steerforth and Ham were also rolled into the whirlpool and disappeared. The sea seemed much calmer than before. There were only a few pieces of broken wood floating there, as if what had just been broken was just a small wooden box, and it seemed that the sea had swallowed many things and two people, and had extinguished its anger and no longer showed its ferocity. (To be continued)
